id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<td>57,188\n</td>\n<td>96,992\n</td>\n<td>107,637\n</td>\n<td>113,732\n</td>\n<td>113,351\n</td>\n<td>112,972\n</td>\n<td>123,185\n</td>\n<td>134,346\n</td>\n<td>144,950\n</td>\n<td>156,421\n</td>\n<td>154,083\n</td>\n<td>164,737\n</td>\n<td>169,045\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>North Somerset<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<td>16,670\n</td>\n<td>33,774\n</td>\n<td>60,066\n</td>\n<td>68,410\n</td>\n<td>75,276\n</td>\n<td>82,833\n</td>\n<td>91,967\n</td>\n<td>102,119\n</td>\n<td>119,509\n</td>\n<td>139,924\n</td>\n<td>160,353\n</td>\n<td>179,865\n</td>\n<td>188,556\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Total\n</th>\n<td><b>261,124</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>407,450</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>445,266</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>462,357</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>471,038</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>479,758</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>520,396</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>563,970</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>619,751</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>682,043</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>731,886</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>812,997</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>855,694</b>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somerset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WestonTownHall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Stone building with colonnaded entrance. Above is a clock tower." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/WestonTownHall.jpg/220px-WestonTownHall.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/WestonTownHall.jpg/330px-WestonTownHall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/WestonTownHall.jpg/440px-WestonTownHall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1590" data-file-height="1168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WestonTownHall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Weston-super-Mare town hall, the administrative headquarters of North Somerset</div></div></div>\n<p>The county is divided into nine constituencies, each returning one Member of Parliament (MP) to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2017" title="United Kingdom general election, 2017">June 2017 general election</a>, the majority of constituencies of the county elected <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> MPs, with the exception of Bath, who elected a <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> <sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The ceremonial county of Somerset contains the constituencies <a href="/wiki/Bridgwater_and_West_Somerset_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bridgwater and West Somerset (UK Parliament constituency)">Bridgwater and West Somerset</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_East_Somerset_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="North East Somerset (UK Parliament constituency)">North East Somerset</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Somerset_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="North Somerset (UK Parliament constituency)">North Somerset</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bath_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bath (UK Parliament constituency)">Bath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somerton_and_Frome_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Somerton and Frome (UK Parliament constituency)">Somerton and Frome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taunton_Deane_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Taunton Deane (UK Parliament constituency)">Taunton Deane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wells_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Wells (UK Parliament constituency)">Wells</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yeovil_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Yeovil (UK Parliament constituency)">Yeovil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Weston-super-Mare_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Weston-super-Mare (UK Parliament constituency)">Weston-super-Mare</a>. Traditionally several of these have been relatively strong constituencies for the Liberal Democrats, with Labour often getting few votes, even in larger towns such as Yeovil.\n</p><p>Residents of Somerset also form part of the electorate for the <a href="/wiki/South_West_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South West England (European Parliament constituency)">South West England</a> constituency for elections to the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somerset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Somerset_County_Council" title="Somerset County Council">Somerset County Council</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_counties_of_England" title="Ceremonial counties of England">ceremonial county</a> of Somerset consists of a two-tier <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_and_non-metropolitan_counties_of_England" title="Metropolitan and non-metropolitan counties of England">non-metropolitan county</a>, which is administered by <a href="/wiki/Somerset_County_Council" title="Somerset County Council">Somerset County Council</a> and five district councils, and two <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authority</a> areas (whose councils combine the functions of a county and a district). The five <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_England" title="Districts of England">districts</a> of Somerset are <a href="/wiki/West_Somerset" title="West Somerset">West Somerset</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Somerset" title="South Somerset">South Somerset</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taunton_Deane" title="Taunton Deane">Taunton Deane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mendip_District" title="Mendip District">Mendip</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sedgemoor" title="Sedgemoor">Sedgemoor</a>. The two unitary authorities \xe2\x80\x94 which were established on 1 April 1996 following the break-up of the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Avon_(county)" title="Avon (county)">county of Avon</a> \xe2\x80\x94 are <a href="/wiki/North_Somerset" title="North Somerset">North Somerset</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bath_and_North_East_Somerset" title="Bath and North East Somerset">Bath &amp; North East Somerset</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> In 2019 West Somerset and Taunton Deane will merge to form <a href="/wiki/Somerset_West_and_Taunton" title="Somerset West and Taunton">Somerset West and Taunton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc29may18_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc29may18-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>These unitary authorities formed part of the <a href="/wiki/Administrative_counties_of_England" title="Administrative counties of England">administrative county</a> of Somerset before the creation of Avon (a county created to cover Bristol and its environs in north Somerset and south Gloucestershire) in 1974. Bath however was a largely independent <a href="/wiki/County_borough" title="County borough">county borough</a> during the existence of the administrative county of Somerset (from 1889 to 1974).\n</p><p>In 2007, proposals to abolish the five district councils in favour of a unitary authority (covering the existing two-tier county) were rejected following local opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/West_Somerset" title="West Somerset">West Somerset</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_districts_by_population" title="List of English districts by population">least populous district</a> (except for the two <i>sui generis</i> districts) in England. In September 2016, West Somerset and Taunton Deane councils agreed in principle to merge the districts into one (with one council) subject to consultation.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> It is planned to achieve this on 1 April 2019 with the first elections to the new council in May 2019. The new district would not be a unitary authority, with Somerset County Council still performing its functions.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_parishes">Civil parishes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somerset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Civil parishes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_civil_parishes_in_Somerset" title="List of civil parishes in Somerset">List of civil parishes in Somerset</a></div>\n<p>Almost all of the county is covered by the lowest/most local form of English local government, the <a href="/wiki/Civil_parishes_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil parishes in England">civil parish</a>, with either a <a href="/wiki/Parish_councils_in_England" title="Parish councils in England">town or parish council</a> (a city council in the instance of Wells) or a <a href="/wiki/Parish_meeting" title="Parish meeting">parish meeting</a>; some parishes group together, with a single council or meeting for the group. The city of Bath (the area of the former county borough) and much of the town of Taunton are <a href="/wiki/Unparished_area" title="Unparished area">unparished areas</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Emergency_services">Emergency services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somerset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Emergency services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>All of the ceremonial county of Somerset is covered by the <a href="/wiki/Avon_and_Somerset_Constabulary" title="Avon and Somerset Constabulary">Avon and Somerset Constabulary</a>, a police force which also covers Bristol and South Gloucestershire. The police force is governed by the elected <a href="/wiki/Avon_and_Somerset_Police_and_Crime_Commissioner" title="Avon and Somerset Police and Crime Commissioner">Avon and Somerset Police and Crime Commissioner</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Devon_and_Somerset_Fire_and_Rescue_Service" title="Devon and Somerset Fire and Rescue Service">Devon and Somerset Fire and Rescue Service</a> was formed in 2007 upon the merger of the Somerset Fire and Rescue Service with its neighbouring Devon service; it covers the area of Somerset County Council as well as the entire ceremonial county of Devon. The unitary districts of North Somerset and Bath &amp; North East Somerset are instead covered by the <a href="/wiki/Avon_Fire_and_Rescue_Service" title="Avon Fire and Rescue Service">Avon Fire and Rescue Service</a>, a service which also covers Bristol and South Gloucestershire. The <a href="/wiki/South_Western_Ambulance_Service" title="South Western Ambulance Service">South Western Ambulance Service</a> covers the entire South West of England, including all of Somerset; prior to February 2013 the unitary districts of Somerset came under the Great Western Ambulance Service, which merged into South Western. The <a href="/wiki/Dorset_and_Somerset_Air_Ambulance" title="Dorset and Somerset Air Ambulance">Dorset and Somerset Air Ambulance</a> is a charitable organisation based in the county.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somerset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Somerset" title="Culture of Somerset">Culture of Somerset</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cathedrale_de_wells_front_ouest.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Large ornate grey stone facade of a building. Symmetrical ith towers either side." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Cathedrale_de_wells_front_ouest.JPG/220px-Cathedrale_de_wells_front_ouest.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Cathedrale_de_wells_front_ouest.JPG/330px-Cathedrale_de_wells_front_ouest.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Cathedrale_de_wells_front_ouest.JPG/440px-Cathedrale_de_wells_front_ouest.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cathedrale_de_wells_front_ouest.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The west front of Wells Cathedral</div></div></div>\n<p>Somerset has traditions of art, music and literature. <a href="/wiki/William_Wordsworth" title="William Wordsworth">Wordsworth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Taylor_Coleridge" title="Samuel Taylor Coleridge">Coleridge</a> wrote while staying in <a href="/wiki/Coleridge_Cottage" title="Coleridge Cottage">Coleridge Cottage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nether_Stowey" title="Nether Stowey">Nether Stowey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-webbio_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-webbio-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\nThe writer <a href="/wiki/Evelyn_Waugh" title="Evelyn Waugh">Evelyn Waugh</a> spent his last years in the village of <a href="/wiki/Combe_Florey" title="Combe Florey">Combe Florey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The novelist <a href="/wiki/John_Cowper_Powys" title="John Cowper Powys">John Cowper Powys</a> (1872\xe2\x80\x931963) lived in the Somerset village of <a href="/wiki/Montacute" title="Montacute">Montacute</a> from 1885 until 1894 and his novels <i>Wood and Stone</i> (1915) and <i><a href="/wiki/A_Glastonbury_Romance" title="A Glastonbury Romance">A Glastonbury Romance</a></i> (1932) are set in Somerset.\n</p><p>Traditional folk music, both song and dance, was important in the agricultural communities. Somerset songs were collected by <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Sharp" title="Cecil Sharp">Cecil Sharp</a> and incorporated into works such as <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Holst" title="Gustav Holst">Holst\'s</a> <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Somerset_Rhapsody&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="A Somerset Rhapsody (page does not exist)">A Somerset Rhapsody</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Halsway_Manor" title="Halsway Manor">Halsway Manor</a> near <a href="/wiki/Williton" title="Williton">Williton</a> is an international centre for folk music. The tradition continues today with groups such as <a href="/wiki/The_Wurzels" title="The Wurzels">The Wurzels</a> specialising in <a href="/wiki/Scrumpy_and_Western" title="Scrumpy and Western">Scrumpy and Western</a> music.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival" title="Glastonbury Festival">Glastonbury Festival of Contemporary Performing Arts</a> takes place most years in Pilton, near Shepton Mallet, attracting over 170,000 music and culture lovers from around the world to see world-famous entertainers.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Big_Green_Gathering" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Green Gathering">Big Green Gathering</a> which grew out of the Green fields at the Glastonbury Festival is held in the Mendip Hills between <a href="/wiki/Charterhouse,_Somerset" title="Charterhouse, Somerset">Charterhouse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Compton_Martin" title="Compton Martin">Compton Martin</a> each summer.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\nThe annual <a href="/wiki/Bath_Literature_Festival" title="Bath Literature Festival">Bath Literature Festival</a> is one of several local festivals in the county; others include the <a href="/wiki/Frome_Festival" title="Frome Festival">Frome Festival</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Trowbridge_Village_Pump_Festival" title="Trowbridge Village Pump Festival">Trowbridge Village Pump Festival</a>, which, despite its name, is held at <a href="/wiki/Farleigh_Hungerford" title="Farleigh Hungerford">Farleigh Hungerford</a> in Somerset. The annual circuit of <a href="/wiki/West_Country_Carnival" title="West Country Carnival">West Country Carnivals</a> is held in a variety of Somerset towns during the autumn, forming a major regional festival, and the largest Festival of Lights in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glastonbury_Tor.jpg" class="image"><img alt="In the distance a small hill with a stone tower on the top. In the foreground flat land with vegetation." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Glastonbury_Tor.jpg/220px-Glastonbury_Tor.jpg" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Glastonbury_Tor.jpg/330px-Glastonbury_Tor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Glastonbury_Tor.jpg/440px-Glastonbury_Tor.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="740" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glastonbury_Tor.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Glastonbury Tor</div></div></div>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Matter_of_Britain" title="Matter of Britain">Arthurian legend</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avalon" title="Avalon">Avalon</a> became associated with <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Tor" title="Glastonbury Tor">Glastonbury Tor</a> when monks at Glastonbury Abbey claimed to have discovered the bones of King Arthur and his queen.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> What is more certain is that Glastonbury was an important religious centre by 700 and claims to be "the oldest above-ground Christian church in the World"<sup id="cite_ref-glastabbey_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-glastabbey-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> situated "in the mystical land of Avalon." The claim is based on dating the founding of the community of monks at AD&#160;63, the year of the legendary visit of Joseph of Arimathea, who was supposed to have brought the Holy Grail.<sup id="cite_ref-glastabbey_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-glastabbey-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> During the Middle Ages there were also important religious sites at <a href="/wiki/Woodspring_Priory" title="Woodspring Priory">Woodspring Priory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muchelney_Abbey" title="Muchelney Abbey">Muchelney Abbey</a>. The present <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Bath_and_Wells" title="Diocese of Bath and Wells">Diocese of Bath and Wells</a> covers Somerset&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 with the exception of the Parish of <a href="/wiki/Abbots_Leigh" title="Abbots Leigh">Abbots Leigh</a> with Leigh Woods in North Somerset&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 and a small area of Dorset. The <a href="/wiki/Cathedra" title="Cathedra">Episcopal seat</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Bath_and_Wells" title="Bishop of Bath and Wells">Bishop of Bath and Wells</a> is now in the Cathedral Church of Saint Andrew in the city of Wells, having previously been at <a href="/wiki/Bath_Abbey" title="Bath Abbey">Bath Abbey</a>. Before the <a href="/wiki/English_Reformation" title="English Reformation">English Reformation</a>, it was a Roman Catholic diocese; the county now falls within the Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Clifton" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Clifton">Diocese of Clifton</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Saint_Benedict" title="Order of Saint Benedict">Benedictine</a> monastery Saint Gregory\'s Abbey, commonly known as <a href="/wiki/Downside_Abbey" title="Downside Abbey">Downside Abbey</a>, is at <a href="/wiki/Stratton-on-the-Fosse" title="Stratton-on-the-Fosse">Stratton-on-the-Fosse</a>, and the ruins of the former <a href="/wiki/Cistercians" title="Cistercians">Cistercian</a> <a href="/wiki/Cleeve_Abbey" title="Cleeve Abbey">Cleeve Abbey</a> are near the village of <a href="/wiki/Washford" title="Washford">Washford</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tyntesfield_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Yellow stone ornate facade of building with lower arched front to the left. In the foreground could flowers in formal garden." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Tyntesfield_1.jpg/220px-Tyntesfield_1.jpg" width="220" height="286" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Tyntesfield_1.jpg/330px-Tyntesfield_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Tyntesfield_1.jpg/440px-Tyntesfield_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="477" data-file-height="621" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tyntesfield_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tyntesfield</div></div></div>\n<p>The county has several museums; those at Bath include the <a href="/wiki/American_Museum_in_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="American Museum in Britain">American Museum in Britain</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Bath_Architecture" title="Museum of Bath Architecture">Museum of Bath Architecture</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Herschel_Museum_of_Astronomy" title="Herschel Museum of Astronomy">Herschel Museum of Astronomy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Jane_Austen_Centre" title="Jane Austen Centre">Jane Austen Centre</a>, and the Roman Baths. Other visitor attractions which reflect the cultural heritage of the county include: <a href="/wiki/Claverton_Pumping_Station" title="Claverton Pumping Station">Claverton Pumping Station</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dunster_Working_Watermill" title="Dunster Working Watermill">Dunster Working Watermill</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Air_Arm_Museum" title="Fleet Air Arm Museum">Fleet Air Arm Museum</a> at Yeovilton, <a href="/wiki/Nunney_Castle" title="Nunney Castle">Nunney Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Helicopter_Museum_(Weston)" title="The Helicopter Museum (Weston)">The Helicopter Museum</a> in Weston-super-Mare, <a href="/wiki/King_John%27s_Hunting_Lodge,_Axbridge" title="King John&#39;s Hunting Lodge, Axbridge">King John\'s Hunting Lodge</a> in <a href="/wiki/Axbridge" title="Axbridge">Axbridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blake_Museum" title="Blake Museum">Blake Museum</a> Bridgwater, Radstock Museum, <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Somerset" title="Museum of Somerset">Museum of Somerset</a> in Taunton, the <a href="/wiki/Somerset_Rural_Life_Museum" title="Somerset Rural Life Museum">Somerset Rural Life Museum</a> in Glastonbury, and <a href="/wiki/Westonzoyland_Pumping_Station_Museum" title="Westonzoyland Pumping Station Museum">Westonzoyland Pumping Station Museum</a>.\n</p><p>Somerset has 11,500 <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed buildings</a>, 523 <a href="/wiki/Scheduled_monument" title="Scheduled monument">scheduled monuments</a>, 192 <a href="/wiki/Protected_area" title="Protected area">conservation areas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> 41 parks and gardens including those at <a href="/wiki/Barrington_Court" title="Barrington Court">Barrington Court</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holnicote_Estate" title="Holnicote Estate">Holnicote Estate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prior_Park_Landscape_Garden" title="Prior Park Landscape Garden">Prior Park Landscape Garden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tintinhull_Garden" title="Tintinhull Garden">Tintinhull Garden</a>, 36 <a href="/wiki/English_Heritage" title="English Heritage">English Heritage</a> sites and 19 <a href="/wiki/National_Trust_for_Places_of_Historic_Interest_or_Natural_Beauty" title="National Trust for Places of Historic Interest or Natural Beauty">National Trust</a> sites,<sup id="cite_ref-rajan_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rajan-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Clevedon_Court" title="Clevedon Court">Clevedon Court</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fyne_Court" title="Fyne Court">Fyne Court</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montacute_House" title="Montacute House">Montacute House</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tyntesfield" title="Tyntesfield">Tyntesfield</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Stembridge_Mill,_High_Ham" title="Stembridge Mill, High Ham">Stembridge Tower Mill</a>, the last remaining thatched windmill in England.<sup id="cite_ref-rajan_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rajan-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Other historic houses in the county which have remained in private ownership or used for other purposes include <a href="/wiki/Halswell_House" title="Halswell House">Halswell House</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marston_Bigot" title="Marston Bigot">Marston Bigot</a>. A key contribution of Somerset architecture is its <a href="/wiki/Somerset_towers" title="Somerset towers">medieval church towers</a>. Jenkins writes, "These structures, with their buttresses, bell-opening tracery and crowns, rank with Nottinghamshire alabaster as England\'s finest contribution to medieval art."<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bath_Rugby" title="Bath Rugby">Bath Rugby</a> play at the <a href="/wiki/Recreation_Ground_(Bath)" title="Recreation Ground (Bath)">Recreation Ground</a> in Bath, and the <a href="/wiki/Somerset_County_Cricket_Club" title="Somerset County Cricket Club">Somerset County Cricket Club</a> are based at the <a href="/wiki/County_Ground,_Taunton" title="County Ground, Taunton">County Ground</a> in Taunton. The county gained its first <a href="/wiki/The_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="The Football League">Football League</a> club in 2003, when <a href="/wiki/Yeovil_Town_F.C." title="Yeovil Town F.C.">Yeovil Town</a> won promotion to <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Third_Division" title="Football League Third Division">Division Three</a> as <a href="/wiki/Football_Conference" class="mw-redirect" title="Football Conference">Football Conference</a> champions.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> They had achieved numerous <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> victories over football League sides in the past 50 years, and since joining the elite they have won promotion again\xe2\x80\x94as <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Two" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Two">League Two</a> champions in 2005. They came close to yet another promotion in 2007, when they reached the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League One">League One</a> playoff final, but lost to <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_F.C." title="Blackpool F.C.">Blackpool</a> at the newly reopened <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>. Yeovil achieved promotion to the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Championship">Championship</a> in 2013 after beating <a href="/wiki/Brentford_F.C." title="Brentford F.C.">Brentford</a> in the playoff final. <a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred_horse_racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Thoroughbred horse racing">Horse racing</a> courses are at <a href="/wiki/Taunton_Racecourse" title="Taunton Racecourse">Taunton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bath_Racecourse" title="Bath Racecourse">Bath</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wincanton_Racecourse" title="Wincanton Racecourse">Wincanton</a>.\n</p><p>In addition to <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of newspapers in the United Kingdom">English national newspapers</a> the county is served by the regional <i><a href="/wiki/Western_Daily_Press" title="Western Daily Press">Western Daily Press</a></i> and local newspapers including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Weston_%26_Somerset_Mercury" title="The Weston &amp; Somerset Mercury">The Weston &amp; Somerset Mercury</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Bath_Chronicle" title="Bath Chronicle">Bath Chronicle</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Chew_Valley_Gazette" title="Chew Valley Gazette">Chew Valley Gazette</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Somerset_County_Gazette" title="Somerset County Gazette">Somerset County Gazette</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Clevedon_Mercury" title="Clevedon Mercury">Clevedon Mercury</a></i> <i><a href="/wiki/Mendip_Times" title="Mendip Times">Mendip Times</a></i>, and the <i>West Somerset Free Press</i>.  Television and radio are provided by BBC Points West and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Somerset" title="BBC Somerset">BBC Somerset</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heart_West_Country" title="Heart West Country">Heart West Country</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Breeze_(Yeovil_%26_South_Somerset)" title="The Breeze (Yeovil &amp; South Somerset)">The Breeze (Yeovil &amp; South Somerset)</a> Yeovil, and <a href="/wiki/ITV_Wales_%26_West" title="ITV Wales &amp; West">HTV</a>, now known as ITV Wales &amp; West Ltd, but still commonly referred to as HTV.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Somerset" title="Flag of Somerset">Flag of Somerset</a>, representing the ceremonial county, has been registered with the <a href="/wiki/Flag_Institute" title="Flag Institute">Flag Institute</a><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> following a competition in July 2013.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somerset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Somerset" title="Transport in Somerset">Transport in Somerset</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bristol_airport_overview.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Bristol_airport_overview.jpg/220px-Bristol_airport_overview.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Bristol_airport_overview.jpg/330px-Bristol_airport_overview.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Bristol_airport_overview.jpg/440px-Bristol_airport_overview.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="534" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bristol_airport_overview.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bristol_Airport" title="Bristol Airport">Bristol Airport</a>, which is located in North Somerset</div></div></div>\n<p>Somerset has 6,531&#160;km (4,058&#160;mi) of roads. The main arterial routes, which include the M5 motorway, <a href="/wiki/A303_road" title="A303 road">A303</a>, <a href="/wiki/A37_road" title="A37 road">A37</a>, <a href="/wiki/A38_road" title="A38 road">A38</a>, <a href="/wiki/A39_road" title="A39 road">A39</a>, A358 and A361 give good access across the county, but many areas can only be accessed via narrow <a href="/wiki/Country_lane" title="Country lane">country lanes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dandsfire_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dandsfire-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Rail services are provided by the <a href="/wiki/West_of_England_Main_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="West of England Main Line">West of England Main Line</a> through <a href="/wiki/Yeovil_Junction_railway_station" title="Yeovil Junction railway station">Yeovil Junction</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bristol_to_Exeter_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Bristol to Exeter Line">Bristol to Exeter Line</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heart_of_Wessex_Line" title="Heart of Wessex Line">Heart of Wessex Line</a> which runs from <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Temple_Meads_railway_station" title="Bristol Temple Meads railway station">Bristol Temple Meads</a> to <a href="/wiki/Weymouth_railway_station" title="Weymouth railway station">Weymouth</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Reading_to_Taunton_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Reading to Taunton Line">Reading to Taunton Line</a>. The key train operator for Somerset is <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Railway_(train_operating_company)" title="Great Western Railway (train operating company)">Great Western Railway</a>, and other services are operated by <a href="/wiki/South_Western_Railway_(train_operating_company)" title="South Western Railway (train operating company)">South Western Railway</a> and <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bristol_Airport" title="Bristol Airport">Bristol Airport</a>, located in North Somerset, provides national and international air services.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Somerset_Coal_Canal" title="Somerset Coal Canal">Somerset Coal Canal</a> was built in the early 19th century to reduce the cost of transportation of coal and other heavy produce.<sup id="cite_ref-hadfield_56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hadfield-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The first 16 kilometres (10&#160;mi), running from a junction with the <a href="/wiki/Kennet_and_Avon_Canal" title="Kennet and Avon Canal">Kennet and Avon Canal</a>, along the <a href="/wiki/Cam_Brook#Cam_Valley" title="Cam Brook">Cam valley</a>, to a terminal basin at <a href="/wiki/Paulton" title="Paulton">Paulton</a>, were in use by 1805, together with several tramways. A planned 11.7&#160;km (7.3&#160;mi) branch to Midford was never built, but in 1815 a tramway was laid along its towing path. In 1871 the tramway was purchased by the <a href="/wiki/Somerset_%26_Dorset_Joint_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Somerset &amp; Dorset Joint Railway">Somerset &amp; Dorset Joint Railway</a> (S&amp;DJR),<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-athill_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-athill-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> and operated until the 1950s.\n</p><p>The 19th century saw improvements to Somerset\'s roads with the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Turnpike_trusts" title="Turnpike trusts">turnpikes</a>, and the building of canals and railways. Nineteenth-century canals included the <a href="/wiki/Bridgwater_and_Taunton_Canal" title="Bridgwater and Taunton Canal">Bridgwater and Taunton Canal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Westport_Canal" title="Westport Canal">Westport Canal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Canal" title="Glastonbury Canal">Glastonbury Canal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chard_Canal" title="Chard Canal">Chard Canal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dunning_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dunning-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hadfield_56-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hadfield-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dorset_and_Somerset_Canal" title="Dorset and Somerset Canal">Dorset and Somerset Canal</a> was proposed, but little of it was ever constructed and it was abandoned in 1803.<sup id="cite_ref-hadfield_56-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hadfield-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Blue_Anchor_-_70021_(aka_70000)_down_South_Wales_Pullman.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Blue_Anchor_-_70021_%28aka_70000%29_down_South_Wales_Pullman.JPG/220px-Blue_Anchor_-_70021_%28aka_70000%29_down_South_Wales_Pullman.JPG" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Blue_Anchor_-_70021_%28aka_70000%29_down_South_Wales_Pullman.JPG/330px-Blue_Anchor_-_70021_%28aka_70000%29_down_South_Wales_Pullman.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Blue_Anchor_-_70021_%28aka_70000%29_down_South_Wales_Pullman.JPG/440px-Blue_Anchor_-_70021_%28aka_70000%29_down_South_Wales_Pullman.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1366" data-file-height="820" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Blue_Anchor_-_70021_(aka_70000)_down_South_Wales_Pullman.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A steam locomotive and carriages, on the <a href="/wiki/West_Somerset_Railway" title="West Somerset Railway">West Somerset Railway</a>, a heritage line of notable length, in spring 2015</div></div></div>\n<p>The usefulness of the canals was short-lived, though some have now been restored for recreation. The 19th century also saw the construction of railways to and through Somerset. The county was served by five <a href="/wiki/Railways_Act_1921" title="Railways Act 1921">pre-1923 Grouping</a> railway companies: the <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Railway" title="Great Western Railway">Great Western Railway</a> (GWR);<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thomas_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thomas-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> a branch of the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Railway" title="Midland Railway">Midland Railway</a> (MR) to <a href="/wiki/Bath_Green_Park_railway_station" title="Bath Green Park railway station">Bath Green Park</a> (and another one to Bristol);<sup id="cite_ref-smith_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smith-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> the Somerset and Dorset Joint Railway,<sup id="cite_ref-thomas_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thomas-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-awdry-237_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awdry-237-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-casserley_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-casserley-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/London_%26_South_Western_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="London &amp; South Western Railway">London &amp; South Western Railway</a> (L&amp;SWR).<sup id="cite_ref-thomas_129-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thomas-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-williams1_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-williams1-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The former main lines of the GWR are still in use today, although many of its branch lines were scrapped as part of the <a href="/wiki/Beeching_cuts" title="Beeching cuts">Beeching cuts</a>. The former lines of the <a href="/wiki/Somerset_%26_Dorset_Joint_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Somerset &amp; Dorset Joint Railway">Somerset &amp; Dorset Joint Railway</a> closed completely,<sup id="cite_ref-atthill_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atthill-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> as has the branch of the Midland Railway to Bath Green Park (and to <a href="/wiki/Bristol_St_Philip%27s_railway_station" title="Bristol St Philip&#39;s railway station">Bristol St Philips</a>); however, the L&amp;SWR survived as a part of the present West of England Main Line. None of these lines, in Somerset, are <a href="/wiki/Railway_electrification_in_Great_Britain" title="Railway electrification in Great Britain">electrified</a>. Two branch lines, the West and <a href="/wiki/East_Somerset_Railway" title="East Somerset Railway">East Somerset Railways</a>, were rescued and transferred back to private ownership as "heritage" lines. The fifth railway was a short-lived light railway, the <a href="/wiki/Weston,_Clevedon_%26_Portishead_Light_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Weston, Clevedon &amp; Portishead Light Railway">Weston, Clevedon &amp; Portishead Light Railway</a>. The <a href="/wiki/West_Somerset_Mineral_Railway" title="West Somerset Mineral Railway">West Somerset Mineral Railway</a> carried the iron ore from the Brendon Hills to Watchet.\n</p><p>Until the 1960s the piers at Weston-super-Mare, Clevedon, Portishead and Minehead were served by the <a href="/wiki/Paddle_steamer" title="Paddle steamer">paddle steamers</a> of <a href="/w/index.php?title=P_and_A_Campbell&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="P and A Campbell (page does not exist)">P and A Campbell</a> who ran regular services to <a href="/wiki/Barry,_Vale_of_Glamorgan" title="Barry, Vale of Glamorgan">Barry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Ilfracombe" title="Ilfracombe">Ilfracombe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lundy" title="Lundy">Lundy Island</a>. The pier at Burnham-on-Sea was used for commercial goods, one of the reasons for the Somerset and Dorset Joint Railway was to provide a link between the Bristol Channel and the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a>. The pier at Burnham-on-Sea is the shortest pier in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-handley_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-handley-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In the 1970s the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Portbury_Dock" title="Royal Portbury Dock">Royal Portbury Dock</a> was constructed to provide extra capacity for the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Bristol" title="Port of Bristol">Port of Bristol</a>.\n</p><p>For long-distance holiday traffic travelling through the county to and from Devon and Cornwall, Somerset is often regarded as a marker on the journey. North\xe2\x80\x93south traffic moves through the county via the M5 Motorway.<sup id="cite_ref-charlesworth_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charlesworth-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Traffic to and from the east travels either via the A303 road, or the M4 Motorway, which runs east\xe2\x80\x93west, crossing the M5 just beyond the northern limits of the county.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somerset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Somerset" title="List of schools in Somerset">List of schools in Somerset</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/State_school" title="State school">State schools</a> in Somerset are provided by three <a href="/wiki/Local_education_authority" title="Local education authority">local education authorities</a>: Bath and North East Somerset, North Somerset, and the larger Somerset County Council. All state schools are comprehensive. In some areas primary, <a href="/wiki/Infant_school" title="Infant school">infant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Junior_school" title="Junior school">junior</a> schools cater for ages four to eleven, after which the pupils move on to secondary schools. There is a <a href="/wiki/Three-tier_education" title="Three-tier education">three-tier system</a> of <a href="/wiki/First_school" title="First school">first</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_school" title="Middle school">middle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Upper_school" title="Upper school">upper</a> schools in the Cheddar Valley,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> and in West Somerset, while most other schools in the county use the two-tier system.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Somerset has 30 state and 17 independent secondary schools;<sup id="cite_ref-somschools_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-somschools-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Bath and North East Somerset has 13 state and 5 independent secondary schools;<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> and North Somerset has 10 state and 2 independent secondary schools, excluding <a href="/wiki/Sixth_form_college" title="Sixth form college">sixth form colleges</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable floatright" style="margin-left: 1em; width: 30em; font-size: 90%;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="2"><b>% of pupils gaining 5 grades A-C including English and Maths in 2006</b> (average for England is 45.8%)\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Education Authority</th>\n<th>%\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Bath and North East Somerset (Unitary Authority)</td>\n<td>52.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>West Somerset</td>\n<td>51.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Taunton Deane</td>\n<td>49.5%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Mendip</td>\n<td>47.7%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>North Somerset (Unitary Authority)</td>\n<td>47.4%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>South Somerset</td>\n<td>42.3%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Sedgemoor</td>\n<td>41.4%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Some of the county\'s secondary schools have <a href="/wiki/Specialist_schools_programme" title="Specialist schools programme">specialist school</a> status. Some schools have sixth forms and others transfer their sixth formers to colleges. Several schools can trace their origins back many years, such as <a href="/wiki/The_Blue_School,_Wells" title="The Blue School, Wells">The Blue School</a> in Wells and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Huish_College,_Taunton" title="Richard Huish College, Taunton">Richard Huish College</a> in Taunton.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> Others have changed their names over the years such as <a href="/wiki/Beechen_Cliff_School" title="Beechen Cliff School">Beechen Cliff School</a> which was started in 1905 as the City of Bath Boys\' School and changed to its present name in 1972 when the <a href="/wiki/Grammar_school" title="Grammar school">grammar school</a> was amalgamated with a local <a href="/wiki/Secondary_modern_school" title="Secondary modern school">secondary modern school</a>, to form a <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_school" title="Comprehensive school">comprehensive school</a>. Many others were established and built since the Second World War. In 2006, 5,900 pupils in Somerset sat <a href="/wiki/General_Certificate_of_Secondary_Education" title="General Certificate of Secondary Education">GCSE</a> examinations, with 44.5% achieving 5 grades A-C including English and Maths (compared to 45.8% for England).\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sexey%27s_School" title="Sexey&#39;s School">Sexey\'s School</a> is a state <a href="/wiki/Boarding_school" title="Boarding school">boarding school</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bruton" title="Bruton">Bruton</a> that also takes day pupils from the surrounding area.<sup id="cite_ref-sexeyshistory_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sexeyshistory-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> The Somerset LEA also provides <a href="/wiki/Special_education#Special_schools" title="Special education">special schools</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Newbury_Manor_School" title="Newbury Manor School">Newbury Manor School</a>, which caters for children aged between 10 and 17 with <a href="/wiki/Special_education_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Special education in the United Kingdom">special educational needs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Provision for pupils with special educational needs is also made by the mainstream schools.\n</p><p>There is also a range of <a href="/wiki/Independent_school_(United_Kingdom)" title="Independent school (United Kingdom)">independent</a> or <a href="/wiki/Public_school_(United_Kingdom)" title="Public school (United Kingdom)">public schools</a>. Many of these are for pupils between 11 and 18 years, such as <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College,_Taunton" title="King&#39;s College, Taunton">King\'s College, Taunton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taunton_School" title="Taunton School">Taunton School</a>. <a href="/wiki/King%27s_School,_Bruton" title="King&#39;s School, Bruton">King\'s School, Bruton</a>, was founded in 1519 and received royal foundation status around 30 years later in the reign of <a href="/wiki/Edward_VI_of_England" title="Edward VI of England">Edward VI</a>. <a href="/wiki/Millfield" title="Millfield">Millfield</a> is the largest <a href="/wiki/Mixed-sex_education" title="Mixed-sex education">co-educational</a> boarding school. There are also <a href="/wiki/Preparatory_school_(United_Kingdom)" title="Preparatory school (United Kingdom)">preparatory schools</a> for younger children, such as <a href="/wiki/All_Hallows_Preparatory_School" title="All Hallows Preparatory School">All Hallows</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hazlegrove_Preparatory_School" title="Hazlegrove Preparatory School">Hazlegrove Preparatory School</a>. <a href="/wiki/Chilton_Cantelo_School" title="Chilton Cantelo School">Chilton Cantelo School</a> offers places both to day pupils and boarders aged 7 to 16. Other schools provide education for children from the age of 3 or 4 years through to 18, such as <a href="/wiki/King_Edward%27s_School,_Bath" title="King Edward&#39;s School, Bath">King Edward\'s School, Bath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_College,_Taunton" title="Queen&#39;s College, Taunton">Queen\'s College, Taunton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wells_Cathedral_School" title="Wells Cathedral School">Wells Cathedral School</a> which is one of the five established musical schools for school-age children in Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Some of these schools have religious affiliations, such as <a href="/wiki/Monkton_Combe_School" title="Monkton Combe School">Monkton Combe School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prior_Park_College" title="Prior Park College">Prior Park College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sidcot_School" title="Sidcot School">Sidcot School</a> which is associated with the <a href="/wiki/Quakers" title="Quakers">Religious Society of Friends</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Downside_School" title="Downside School">Downside School</a> which is a Roman Catholic public school in Stratton-on-the-Fosse, situated next to the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Saint_Benedict" title="Order of Saint Benedict">Benedictine</a> Downside Abbey,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kingswood_School" title="Kingswood School">Kingswood School</a>, which was founded by <a href="/wiki/John_Wesley" title="John Wesley">John Wesley</a> in 1748 in Kingswood near Bristol, originally for the education of the sons of the itinerant ministers (clergy) of the <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodist Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_and_higher_education">Further and higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somerset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Further and higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A wide range of <a href="/wiki/Adult_education" title="Adult education">adult education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">further education</a> courses is available in Somerset, in schools, colleges and other community venues. The colleges include <a href="/wiki/Weston_College" title="Weston College">Weston College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bridgwater_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Bridgwater College">Bridgwater and Taunton College</a> (formed in 2016 when Bridgwater College and <a href="/wiki/Somerset_College_of_Arts_and_Technology" title="Somerset College of Arts and Technology">Somerset College of Arts and Technology</a> merged, and includes the Taunton-based University Centre Somerset), <a href="/wiki/Bath_College" title="Bath College">Bath College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frome_Community_College" title="Frome Community College">Frome Community College</a>, Richard Huish College, <a href="/wiki/Strode_College" title="Strode College">Strode College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yeovil_College" title="Yeovil College">Yeovil College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Somerset County Council operates <a href="/wiki/Dillington_House" title="Dillington House">Dillington House</a>, a residential adult education college located in Ilminster.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bath" title="University of Bath">University of Bath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bath_Spa_University" title="Bath Spa University">Bath Spa University</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_Centre_Weston" title="University Centre Weston">University Centre Weston</a> are higher education establishments in the north of the county. The University of Bath gained its Royal Charter in 1966, although its origins go back to the Bristol Trade School (founded 1856) and Bath School of Pharmacy (founded 1907).<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> It has a purpose-built campus at <a href="/wiki/Claverton,_Somerset" title="Claverton, Somerset">Claverton</a> on the outskirts of Bath, and has 15,000 students.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Bath Spa University, which is based at <a href="/wiki/Newton_St_Loe" title="Newton St Loe">Newton St Loe</a>, achieved university status in 2005, and has origins including the Bath Academy of Art (founded 1898), Bath Teacher Training College, and the Bath College of Higher Education.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> It has several campuses and 5,500 students.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Somerset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" title="Belmarsh prison">Belmarsh prison</a> in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span
